       <article class="post-290 post type-post status-publish format-standard category-installation-wordpress-shopping-cart tag-installation tag-wp-shopping-cart entry" itemscope itemtype="https://schema.org/CreativeWork">
        <header class="entry-header">
         <h1 class="entry-title" itemprop="headline">Simple WP Shopping Cart Installation and Usage Instructions</h1> 
        </header>
        <div class="entry-content" itemprop="text">
         <p><iframe width="500" height="281" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/tEZWfTmZ2kk?feature=oembed" frameborder="0" allowfullscreen></iframe></p> 
         <h2>WP Shopping Cart Installation</h2> 
         <ol> 
          <li>Unzip and Upload the folder “wordpress-paypal-shopping-cart” to the “/wp-content/plugins/” directory.</li> 
          <li>Activate the plugin through the “Plugins” menu in WordPress.</li> 
          <li>Go to Settings and configure the options (eg. your paypal email, Shopping Cart name, Return URL etc.)</li> 
          <li>Use the shortcode to add a product to a post or page where you want it to appear.</li> 
         </ol> 
         <h2>WP Shopping Cart Basic Usage</h2> 
         <p><strong>Step 1:</strong> To add the ‘Add to Cart’ button simply insert the following shortcode to a post or page next to the product description:</p> 
         <p><code>[wp_cart_button name="PRODUCT-NAME" price="PRODUCT-PRICE"]</code></p> 
         <p>Replace PRODUCT-NAME and PRODUCT-PRICE with the actual name and price.</p> 
         <p>Here is an example usage of the shortcode:</p> 
         <p><code>[wp_cart_button name="Test Product" price="19.95"]</code></p> 
         <p><strong>Step 2:</strong> To add the shopping cart to a post or page, insert the following shortcode to a post or page.</p> 
         <p><code>[show_wp_shopping_cart]</code></p> 
         <h2>Using the Buttons and Cart From a template file</h2> 
         <p>If you want to add a purchase button in your theme’s template file then do the following:</p> 
         <p>1. To add the ‘Add to Cart’ button from template (.php) files use the following function:</p> 
         <pre>&lt;?php echo print_wp_cart_button_for_product('PRODUCT-NAME', PRODUCT-PRICE); ?&gt;</pre> 
         <p>Replace PRODUCT-NAME and PRODUCT-PRICE with the actual name and price. Example:</p> 
         <pre>&lt;?php echo print_wp_cart_button_for_product('wordpress', 7.50); ?&gt;
</pre> 
         <p>2. To add the shopping cart to the sidebar, simply use the widget from the widgets menu or add the following line to your sidebar template file where you want the shopping cart to appear.</p> 
         <pre>&lt;?php echo print_wp_shopping_cart() ?&gt;</pre> 
         <h2>Display a Product Box</h2> 
         <p>Read the following documentation that explains how you can use a shortcode to display a nice product box for your product(s):</p> 
         <ul> 
          <li><a href="https://www.tipsandtricks-hq.com/ecommerce/how-to-show-a-product-display-box-2278">How to display a product box</a></li> 
         </ul> 
         <h2>Example Post/Page Editor Content with Shortcode</h2> 
         <p>The following is a screenshot of the WordPress post/page editor showing how the ‘add to cart’ button and the shopping cart is inserted into a post or page.</p> 
         <p><img class="alignnone size-full wp-image-2481" src="https://www.tipsandtricks-hq.com/ecommerce/wp-content/uploads/2009/07/simple-cart-wp-editor-content-example.png" alt="simple cart wp editor content example" width="444" height="337" srcset="https://www.tipsandtricks-hq.com/ecommerce/wp-content/uploads/2009/07/simple-cart-wp-editor-content-example.png 444w, https://www.tipsandtricks-hq.com/ecommerce/wp-content/uploads/2009/07/simple-cart-wp-editor-content-example-300x227.png 300w" sizes="(max-width: 444px) 100vw, 444px"></p> 
         <h2>Using a Compact Shopping Cart</h2> 
         <p>Use the following shortcode where you want to show the compact shopping cart:<br> <code><br> [wp_compact_cart]<br> </code><br> You can add this shortcode in a standard text widget to add the compact cart to the sidebar.</p> 
         <h2>Always Show the Shopping Cart</h2> 
         <p>The standard “show_wp_shopping_cart” shortcode only shows the cart when there are items in the cart. So it shows the cart when the visitor has clicked on an add to cart button and added item(s) to the cart. When the cart is empty, it simply hides the cart (nothing is shown).</p> 
         <p>If you want to show the cart all the time then use the following shortcode instead. It will show an empty cart message when there is nothing in the cart.</p> 
         <pre>[always_show_wp_shopping_cart]
</pre> 
         <h2>Using Shipping Option</h2> 
         <p>1. To use shipping cost use the “shipping” argument in the shortcode. Here is an example usage:</p> 
         <pre>[wp_cart_button name="Test Product" price="19.95" shipping="4.99"]</pre> 
         <p>or use the following php function from your wordpress template files</p> 
         <pre>&lt;?php echo print_wp_cart_button_for_product('product name',price,shipping cost); ?&gt;</pre> 
         <p>Please see the <a href="https://www.tipsandtricks-hq.com/ecommerce/wordpress-shopping-cart-how-the-shipping-cost-calculation-works-297">How shipping Calculation Works</a> post for more info.</p> 
         <h2>Using Variation Control Option</h2> 
         <p><iframe width="500" height="281" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/9NxDgldBEQE?feature=oembed" frameborder="0" allowfullscreen></iframe></p> 
         <p>Variation Control can be used to create products similar to the following screenshot:</p> 
         <p><img class="alignnone size-full wp-image-317" title="wp-shopping-cart-prodcut-variation-sample" src="https://www.tipsandtricks-hq.com/ecommerce/wp-content/uploads/2009/07/wp-shopping-cart-prodcut-variation-sample.jpg" alt="wp-shopping-cart-prodcut-variation-sample" width="209" height="241"></p> 
         <div id="attachment_347" style="width: 440px" class="wp-caption alignnone">
          <img class="size-full wp-image-347" title="wp-shopping-cart-with-variation-control" src="http://www.tipsandtricks-hq.com/ecommerce/wp-content/uploads/2009/07/wp-shopping-cart-with-variation-control.JPG" alt="wp-shopping-cart-with-variation-control" width="430" height="260" srcset="https://www.tipsandtricks-hq.com/ecommerce/wp-content/uploads/2009/07/wp-shopping-cart-with-variation-control.JPG 430w, https://www.tipsandtricks-hq.com/ecommerce/wp-content/uploads/2009/07/wp-shopping-cart-with-variation-control-300x181.jpg 300w" sizes="(max-width: 430px) 100vw, 430px">
          <p class="wp-caption-text">Shopping Cart Screenshot with Variation Control</p>
         </div> 
         <p><strong>1.</strong> To use variation control for your product use the variation argument like the following:</p> 
         <p>[wp_cart_button name=”Test Product” price=”25.95? var1=”VARIATION-NAME|VARIATION1|VARIATION2|VARIATION3?]</p> 
         <p>Here is an example usage:</p> 
         <p>[wp_cart_button name=”Test Product” price=”29.95? var1=”Size|small|medium|large”]</p> 
         <p><strong>2.</strong> To use a 2nd or 3rd variation use the following:</p> 
         <p>[wp_cart_button name=”Test Product” price=”29.95? var1=”Size|small|medium|large” var2=”Color|red|green|blue”]</p> 
         <p>[wp_cart_button name=”Test Product” price=”29.95? var1=”Size|small|medium|large” var2=”Color|red|green|blue” var3=”Sleeve|short|full”]</p> 
         <h2>Selling Digital Media Files</h2> 
         <p>See the <a href="https://www.tipsandtricks-hq.com/ecommerce/wp-simple-cart-sell-digital-downloads-2468">media file selling usage</a> documentation.</p> 
         <h2>Use an User Interface to Insert the Shortcodes</h2> 
         <p>The plugin has a shortcode inserter that you can use to add the shortcodes to your WordPress posts/pages.</p> 
         <p>Feel free to leave a comment below if you are having any difficulties.</p> 
         <p>Visit the <a href="https://www.tipsandtricks-hq.com/wordpress-simple-paypal-shopping-cart-plugin-768">WordPress Shopping Cart</a> Plugin Page.</p> 
         <div class="custom_yellow_box">
          <p><strong>Note:</strong> We now provide technical support for our premium plugins via our <a href="https://www.tipsandtricks-hq.com/forum/" target="_blank"><u>customer only support forum</u></a></p>
         </div>

           <p>The following function should do the job to calculate the number of items in the shopping cart:</p> 
           <pre>function simple_cart_total_itmes()
{
    $total = 0;
    foreach ($_SESSION['simpleCart'] as $item)
    {
        $total ++;
    }
    return $total;
}
</pre>

Please note PayPal does have a limitation on the characters that can be passed (320 this includes the name of the product and the variation).</p>

         <li class="comment odd alt thread-odd thread-alt depth-1" id="comment-1570"> 
          <div class="comment-header"> 
           <div class="comment-author vcard"> 
            <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/20ff337979693e6f9786d51f47c9dbec?s=48&amp;d=identicon&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/20ff337979693e6f9786d51f47c9dbec?s=96&amp;d=identicon&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-48 photo" height="48" width="48"> 
            <cite class="fn">Dave Y.</cite> 
            <span class="says">says:</span> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div class="comment-content"> 
           <p>Thanks so much for the plug-in. I got it working in no time. I wanted to pass along some code to some fellow users that may be helpful.</p> 
           <p>Let’s say you hard coded the Add to Cart code on your template file and need to change the price for individual products on individual pages or posts. You can do so by using a WordPress Custom Field. The following example works the the custom field of “price”.</p> 
           <p>&amp;alt;?php $price = get_post_meta( $post-&gt;ID, ‘price’, true ); ?&gt;<br> ^^^Above the loop in the template</p> 
           <p>&amp;alt;?php echo print_wp_cart_button_for_product($name, $price); ?&gt;<br> ^^^In your template</p> 
           <p>I hope this can help someone and I’d love to hear Ruhul’s input.</p> 
          </div> 
          <div class="reply"> 
          </div> </li>

           <p>Follow-up on the “Visit The Shop” suggestion. I did find a better work around than editing the wp_shopping_cart.php. I simply put the link into the “Text to show when Cart empty” setting: </p> 
           <p> Visit <a href="mysite.org/members.php" rel="nofollow">Member Services</a></p> 
           <p>It works fine, but breaks the settings page display of that field, probably because of the unexpected HTML. </p> 
           <p>Thanks again for a great plugin!</p>

            <cite class="fn">admin</cite>

           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div class="comment-content"> 
           <p>@Michael, please make sure you don’t use any symbol in your price field including comma (,). Only use the number eg. 49.99 (PayPal doesn’t like symbols in the price field.</p> 
           <p>Regarding the variation… you need to make sure your themes footer.php has a call to the wp_footer() function or it won’t add the javascripts. Many themes are not designed according to WordPress standard and causes problems. The following URL should help:</p> 
           <p><a href="http://www.tipsandtricks-hq.com/ecommerce/wp-shopping-cart-troubleshooting-578" rel="nofollow">http://www.tipsandtricks-hq.com/ecommerce/wp-shopping-cart-troubleshooting-578</a></p> 
          </div>

           <p>add_filter(‘the_content’, ‘print_wp_cart_button_new’,11);</p> 
           <p>11 is the filter priority.. you can change that to whatever you like.</p>

           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div class="comment-content"> 
           <p>Hi Beth, You need to add the trigger text that displays the shopping cart when items are added in the cart so customers can checkout. Please refer to the 3rd and 4th instructions on the Usage Instructions on this page.</p> 
           <p>You can add a reference text input box to collect user input using the “on1” and “os1” optional PayPal HTML Variables. Simply add a input text box and put the value of this to the “os1” field and add to the paypal form that gets submitted during checkout.</p> 
          </div>

          <div class="comment-content"> 
           <p>Hi Rich, you seem to have the following in your theme’s CSS file: </p> 
           <p>select {<br> width: 130px;<br> }</p> 
           <p>This is why it’s making the “select” input fields 130px wide. remove the width or the whole select block and it will adjust to the size of the text.</p>

         <li class="comment byuser comment-author-admin bypostauthor odd alt thread-odd thread-alt depth-1" id="comment-696"> 
          <div class="comment-header"> 
           <div class="comment-author vcard"> 
            <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/7bd856fabb779a6cad044c59a17ca321?s=48&amp;d=identicon&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/7bd856fabb779a6cad044c59a17ca321?s=96&amp;d=identicon&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-48 photo" height="48" width="48"> 
            <cite class="fn">admin</cite> 
            <span class="says">says:</span> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div class="comment-content"> 
           <p>Hi Dom, if you have multiple page styles then you will need to specify the one you want to use for this site by adding an input field like the one below in the shopping cart checkout form:</p> 
           <p>&lt;input type=”hidden” name=”page_style” value=”PayPal”&gt;</p> 
           <p>“PayPal” here is the default one… change this to the name of your page style.</p> 
           <p>Please note that the trigger text only work in a post or a page. If you want to use something from the sidebar then you will have to use the respective PHP function call specified in the documentation.</p> 
          </div> 
          <div class="reply"> 
          </div> </li>

            <cite class="fn">admin</cite> 
            <span class="says">says:</span> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div class="comment-content"> 
           <p>Hi John, You are confusing the WP eStore changelog with the simple shopping cart one (Pay attention to the title of the post). Please note that there are two plugins WP eStore (this allows your to restrict the number of items available) and WP Simple Shopping Cart (this does not have that functionality). Alec’s question was in regards to the simple shopping cart plugin.</p> 
           <p>The simple wp shopping cart plugin doesn’t have this functionality because it doesn’t use a database to store the product details and hence it can’t keep track of the number of items sold. I have many thousands of users of this plugin who like it because it’s very light-weight and simple to use and I plan to keep it that way.</p> 
          </div> 
          <div class="reply"> 
          </div> </li>

         <li class="comment byuser comment-author-admin bypostauthor even thread-even depth-1" id="comment-296"> 
          <div class="comment-header"> 
           <div class="comment-author vcard"> 
            <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/7bd856fabb779a6cad044c59a17ca321?s=48&amp;d=identicon&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/7bd856fabb779a6cad044c59a17ca321?s=96&amp;d=identicon&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-48 photo" height="48" width="48"> 
            <cite class="fn">admin</cite> 
            <span class="says">says:</span> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div class="comment-content"> 
           <p>@Tim, when you click the “add to cart” button it adds the item to the shopping cart on your site. Customers can add more products to the shopping cart or delete items from it. It takes them to the PayPal page for payment when they click the “Checkout” button on the shopping cart. You seem to be missing the shopping cart part. Please follow the instructions and add the shopping cart to your sidebar using the widget or to a post or page using the trigger text. This way when someone clicks the “Add to Cart” button their item(s) will be displayed in the shopping cart. Let me know if that helps.</p> 
          </div> 
          <div class="reply"> 
          </div> </li>

         <li class="comment byuser comment-author-admin bypostauthor even thread-even depth-1" id="comment-237"> 
          <div class="comment-header"> 
           <div class="comment-author vcard"> 
            <img alt="" src="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/7bd856fabb779a6cad044c59a17ca321?s=48&amp;d=identicon&amp;r=g" srcset="https://secure.gravatar.com/avatar/7bd856fabb779a6cad044c59a17ca321?s=96&amp;d=identicon&amp;r=g 2x" class="avatar avatar-48 photo" height="48" width="48"> 
            <cite class="fn">admin</cite> 
            <span class="says">says:</span> 
           </div> 
          </div> 
          <div class="comment-content"> 
           <p>@Dave, If you display the shopping cart on a different page (eg. checkout page) than where the ‘Add to Cart’ buttons are then you won’t have any problem even if your theme is loading the Javascript files in the header. </p> 
           <p>Anyway, to load the javascript files in the footer you need to simply copy the line of text that’s loading the javascript file from the ‘header.php’ file to the ‘footer.php’ file. in your header.php file you will see lines similar to the following that loads the javascript file:<br> &lt;script type=”text/javascript” src=”http://www.your-domain.com/wp-content/themes/your-theme-name/script-name.js”&gt;&lt;/script&gt;</p> 
           <p>so just search for the following text and move that line to the footer.php<br> &lt;script type=”text/javascript”</p> 
           <p>Hope that helps.</p> 
          </div> 
          <div class="reply"> 
          </div> </li>

  <!-- WP Audio player plugin v1.9.6 - https://www.tipsandtricks-hq.com/wordpress-audio-music-player-plugin-4556/ --> 
  <script type="text/javascript">
        soundManager.useFlashBlock = true; // optional - if used, required flashblock.css
        soundManager.url = 'https://www.tipsandtricks-hq.com/ecommerce/wp-content/plugins/compact-wp-audio-player/swf/soundmanager2.swf';
        function play_mp3(flg, ids, mp3url, volume, loops)
        {
            //Check the file URL parameter value
            var pieces = mp3url.split("|");
            if (pieces.length > 1) {//We have got an .ogg file too
                mp3file = pieces[0];
                oggfile = pieces[1];
                //set the file URL to be an array with the mp3 and ogg file
                mp3url = new Array(mp3file, oggfile);
            }

            soundManager.createSound({
                id: 'btnplay_' + ids,
                volume: volume,
                url: mp3url
            });

            if (flg == 'play') {
                    soundManager.play('btnplay_' + ids, {
                    onfinish: function() {
                        if (loops == 'true') {
                            loopSound('btnplay_' + ids);
                        }
                        else {
                            document.getElementById('btnplay_' + ids).style.display = 'inline';
                            document.getElementById('btnstop_' + ids).style.display = 'none';
                        }
                    }
                });
            }
            else if (flg == 'stop') {
    //soundManager.stop('btnplay_'+ids);
                soundManager.pause('btnplay_' + ids);
            }
        }
        function show_hide(flag, ids)
        {
            if (flag == 'play') {
                document.getElementById('btnplay_' + ids).style.display = 'none';
                document.getElementById('btnstop_' + ids).style.display = 'inline';
            }
            else if (flag == 'stop') {
                document.getElementById('btnplay_' + ids).style.display = 'inline';
                document.getElementById('btnstop_' + ids).style.display = 'none';
            }
        }
        function loopSound(soundID)
        {
            window.setTimeout(function() {
                soundManager.play(soundID, {onfinish: function() {
                        loopSound(soundID);
                    }});
            }, 1);
        }
        function stop_all_tracks()
        {
            soundManager.stopAll();
            var inputs = document.getElementsByTagName("input");
            for (var i = 0; i < inputs.length; i++) {
                if (inputs[i].id.indexOf("btnplay_") == 0) {
                    inputs[i].style.display = 'inline';//Toggle the play button
                }
                if (inputs[i].id.indexOf("btnstop_") == 0) {
                    inputs[i].style.display = 'none';//Hide the stop button
                }
            }
        }
    </script>

   <div class="cart_redirection_contentWrap"></div>
  </div>
  <script type="text/javascript">
jQuery.noConflict();
jQuery(document).ready(function($) {
$(function() {
	//set this cookie value according to the T and C settings.
	if ($(".t-and-c").length > 0){	
		if(!$(".t-and-c").is(':checked')){
			$.cookie("eStore_submit_payment","false",{path: '/'});						
		}
	}
	else{
		$.cookie("eStore_submit_payment","true",{path: '/'});
	}	
	$(".redirect_trigger").overlay({
		mask: '#3D4752',
		effect: 'apple',
		target:$('.eStore_apple_overlay'),
		top: '20%',		
 
		onBeforeLoad: function() {
			// grab wrapper element inside content
			var wrap = this.getOverlay().find(".cart_redirection_contentWrap"); 			
			// load the page specified in the trigger
			wrap.load(this.getTrigger().attr("href"));	

			if ($(".t-and-c").length > 0){	
				if(!$(".t-and-c").is(':checked'))
				{
					$.cookie("eStore_submit_payment","false",{path: '/'});	
					wrap.close();						
				}
			}	 
		} 
	}); 
 });
 });
</script>

  <script type="text/javascript">
jQuery.noConflict();
jQuery(document).ready(function($) {
$(function() {
	var shipping_var_warning_class = $('.shipping_var_changed');
	var shipping_var_warning_default_class = $('.shipping_var_changed_default');
	shipping_var_warning_class.hide();
	$('.shipping_variation').change(function(){
		shipping_var_warning_default_class.hide();
		shipping_var_warning_class.show();
	});
	var eStore_shipping_var_needs_update = false;
	if(shipping_var_warning_class.is(":visible")){eStore_shipping_var_needs_update = true;}
	else if(shipping_var_warning_default_class.is(":visible")){eStore_shipping_var_needs_update = true;}	
	$(".eStore_paypal_checkout_button").click(function(e){//Check if shipping variation has been selected
		if(eStore_shipping_var_needs_update){
	    	shipping_var_warning_class.css({'border':'1px solid red','padding':'5px'});
	    	shipping_var_warning_default_class.css({'border':'1px solid red','padding':'5px'});
	    	e.preventDefault();
		}
	});	
 });
 });
</script>
